            function wpSolutionToggle(solution, link, showtext, hidetext) {
                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';
                    link.innerHTML = showtext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';
                } else {
                    solution.style.display = 'block';
                    link.innerHTML = hidetext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_hide';
                }
            }

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

								<div class="post-23 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-23">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>1.4 &#8212; A first look at functions</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on May 31st, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>A <strong>function</strong> is a reusable sequence of statements designed to do a particular job.  You already know that every program must have a function named main() (which is the where the program starts execution).  However, most programs use many functions.</p>
<p>Often, your program needs to interrupt what it is doing to temporarily do something else.  You do this in real life all the time.  For example, you might be reading a book when you remember you need to make a phone call.  You put a bookmark in your book, make the phone call, and when you are done with the phone call, you return to your book where you left off.</p>
<p>C++ programs work the same way.  A program will be executing statements sequentially inside one function when it encounters a function call.  A <strong>function call</strong> is an expression that tells the CPU to interrupt the current function and execute another function.  The CPU &#8220;puts a bookmark&#8221; at the current point of execution, and then <strong>calls</strong> (executes) the function named in the function call.  When the called function terminates, the CPU goes back to the point it bookmarked, and resumes execution.</p>
<p>Here is a sample program that shows how new functions are defined and called:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0023 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This program produces the following output:</p>
<pre>
Starting main()
In doPrint()
Ending main()
</pre>
<p>This program begins execution at the top of function main(), and the first line to be executed prints <code>Starting main()</code>.  The second line in main is a function call to the function doPrint().  At this point, execution of statements in main() is suspended, and the CPU jumps to doPrint().  The first (and only) line in doPrint prints <code>In doPrint()</code>.  When doPrint() terminates, the caller (main()) resumes execution where it left off.  Consequently, the next statement executed in main prints <code>Ending main()</code>.</p>
<p>Note that function calls are made by using the function name, plus a parameter list enclosed in parenthesis ().  In this case, since none of our functions use parameters, the list is empty.  We&#8217;ll talk more about function parameters in the next lesson.  If you forget the parameters list, the function will not be called!</p>
<p><strong>Return values</strong></p>
<p>If you remember, when main finishes executing, it returns an integer value back to the operating system (the caller) by using a return statement.</p>
<p>Functions you write can return a single value to their caller as well.  We do this by setting the <strong>return type</strong> of the function in the function&#8217;s definition.  The return type is the type declared before the function name.</p>
<p>A return type of <strong>void</strong> means the function does not return a value.  A return type of int means the function returns an integer value to the caller.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-18"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// prints 5</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-19"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">return5</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">2</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// prints 7</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-20"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">returnNothing</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// This line will not compile.&nbsp;&nbsp;You'll need to comment it out to continue.</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-21">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-22"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">returnNothing</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// okay: function returnNothing() is called, no value is returned</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-23"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">return5</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// okay: function return5() is called, return value is discarded</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9338643018908-24"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0026 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In the first function call, return5() is executed.  The function returns the value of 5 back to the caller, which passes that value to cout.</p>
<p>In the second function call, return5() is executed and returns the value of 5 back to the caller.  The expression 5 + 2 is then evaluated to 7.  The value of 7 is passed to cout.</p>
<p>In the third function call, returnNothing() returns void.  It is not valid to pass void to cout, and the compiler will give you an error when you try to compile this line.  You&#8217;ll need to comment out this line of code in order to make your code compile.</p>
<p>In the fourth function call, returnNothing() is executed.  The function does nothing and returns nothing, so control returns to main().</p>
<p>In the fifth function call, return5() is executed.  The value 5 is returned to main(), but main() does nothing with the return value so the return value is discarded.</p>
<p>One commonly asked question is, &#8220;Can my function return multiple values using a return statement?&#8221;.  The answer is no.  Functions can only return a single value using a return statement.  However, there are ways to work around the issue, which we will discuss when we get into the in-depth section on functions.</p>
<p><strong>Returning to main</strong></p>
<p>You now have the conceptual tools to understand how the main() function actually works.  When the program is executed, the operating system makes a function call to main().  Execution then jumps to the top of main.  The statements in main are executed sequentially.  Finally, main returns a integer value (usually 0) back to the operating system.  This is why main is defined as <code>int main()</code>.</p>
<p>Some compilers will let you get away with defining main as <code>void main()</code>.  Technically this is illegal.  When these compilers see <code>void main()</code>, they interpret it as:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-5">5</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// your code here</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9341893266888-5"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>You should always define main as returning an int and your main function should return 0 (or another integer if there was an error).</p>
<p>For now, you should also define your main() function at the bottom of your code file.  We&#8217;ll talk about why shortly, in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/">1.7 -- Forward Declarations</a>.</p>
<p><strong>Reusing functions</strong></p>
<p>The same function can be called multiple times, which is useful if you need to do something more than once.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0031 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This program produces the following output:</p>
<pre>
Enter an integer: 5
Enter an integer: 7
5 + 7 = 12
</pre>
<p>In this case, main() is interrupted 2 times, once for each call to getValueFromUser().  Note that in both cases, the value read into variable a is passed back to main() via the function&#8217;s return value and then assigned to variable x or y!</p>
<p>Note that main() isn&#8217;t the only function that can call other functions.  Any function can call another function!</p>

class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-1"><span class="crayon-c">//#include &lt;stdafx.h&gt; // Visual Studio users need to uncomment this line</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-2"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;iostream&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-3">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-4"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">printA</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-5"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"A"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-7"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-8">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-9"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">printB</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-10"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-11"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"B"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-12"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-13">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-14"><span class="crayon-c">// function printAB() calls both printA() and printB()</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-15"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">printAB</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-16"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-17"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">printA</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-18"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">printB</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-19"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-20">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-21"><span class="crayon-c">// Definition of main()</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-22"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-23"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-24"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">using</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-25"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Starting main()"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-26"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">printAB</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-27"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Ending main()"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-28"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc934f063941490-29"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0032 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This program produces the following output:</p>
<pre>
Starting main()
A
B
Ending main()
</pre>
<p><strong>Nested functions</strong></p>
<p>Functions can not be defined inside other functions (called nesting) in C++.  The following program is not legal:</p>

nested inside main(), which is illegal.</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9356758836001-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fc9356758836001-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>

<p>The proper way to write the above program is:</p>

	<h3 id="comments">128 comments to 1.4 &#8212; A first look at functions</h3>

		<p>I noticed you include this comment <i>we need this in each function that uses cout and endl</i> when you include namespace std;.</p>
<p>Why do you include the library locally as opposed to globally?  Are there functions in the library that conflict with other libraries that would cause a problem?  Is it just a matter of preference?  I hope I am not getting ahead of myself here.</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-10">
		<div id="div-comment-10" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-10">
		May 31, 2007 at 7:16 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=10#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-10", "10", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>That&#8217;s a very good question, actually.</p>
<p>Just as with local/global variables, it&#8217;s better to declare things at a local scope if you can (and it&#8217;s not too onerous).  It reduces the chance of inadvertently changing something you didn&#8217;t mean to, or having a name clash.</p>
<p>While this is rarely a problem in small programs, in gigantic programs that run ten or hundreds of thousands of lines of code, your odds of having a strange name clash go up significantly.</p>
<p>Probably the safest solution is to not use a &#8220;using&#8221; statement at all, and explicitly call the function with it&#8217;s namespace qualifier:</p>
<p>std::cout << &#8220;Hello world!&#8221; << std::endl;</p>
<p>But that makes for some ugly, harder to read code (and I haven&#8217;t covered the scope qualifier yet!).  Using a using statement at the function level is a nice compromise between safety and readability.</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-4 clearfix" id="comment-251103">
		<div id="div-comment-251103" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251103">
		January 9, 2015 at 3:33 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251103#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251103", "251103", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Generally you won&#8217;t want to merge libraries together.  Libraries are generally designed to provide a set of functionality to do a specific job.  Say for example you have a math library, and a sound library.  It wouldn&#8217;t really make sense to put them together.  And even if you did, it wouldn&#8217;t resolve the naming conflict (you&#8217;d just move the naming conflict into the library itself instead of in your program).</p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>Thanks for the complements, and your question isn&#8217;t silly at all.  If you wanted to compile these fragments, you&#8217;d need to add <code>using namespace std;</code> as well as <code>#include &lt;iostream&gt;</code>, but since they&#8217;re just code fragments rather than entire programs meant to be compiled I omitted the minor details.</p>

		</div>
		<p>I come from a pretty decent background.  I have had 7 years experience in my overall field.  I know PHP/Javascript like the back of my hand&#8230;I wanted to get into C++ lately and I am working towards it.  So far I love the language.  The ONE thing I don&#8217;t like so far about it is having to put the main function at the bottom (or the other way you mentioned).  It seems kind of unnecessary and definitely doesn&#8217;t sound like it&#8217;ll be very neat and manageable. The hard part is remebring to make a function before that&#8230;the one problem I would have is if I had 2 functions that called each other.<br />
In PHP you can have 1 function and then another function and because they are related sometimes each one of the functions ends up calling the OTHER function once.  So that leaves you with something you can&#8217;t do in C++.  You can&#8217;t make both functions above each other (impossible) so it won&#8217;t work like that.</p>
		</div>

		<p>You actually can have two functions in C++ that call each other.  However, to do this, you have to use function prototypes, which we I haven&#8217;t covered at this point in the tutorials.  I cover this in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/" rel="nofollow">1.7 -- forward declarations</a></p>

		<p>After studying your first couple of steps over night this is the code I managed to compile. Mind you I just started last night and never knew a thing about coding until now. I put did a combination of the three tests and heres what I came up with. It was very much enjoyable debugging and learning that the void must come before the main.  Only takes one mind to expand a thousand others, thanks Alex much appreciated, cant wait to study further!<br />
________________________________________________</p>
<p>// Test subject.cpp : main project file.</p>
<p>#include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;<br />
#include </p>
<p>using namespace System;</p>
<p>void Test()<br />
{<br />
	using namespace std;<br />
	cout  &lt;&lt;       &#8220;Starting Test 2&#8243;      &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt;       &#8220;What is the value of X x Y?&#8221;      &lt;&gt; x;<br />
	cin &gt;&gt;y;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt;     &#8220;The correct answer is &#8221;   &lt;&lt; x + y &lt;&lt;endl;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt;       &#8220;Testing complete!&#8221;       &lt;&lt;endl;</p>
<p>	system (&#8220;pause&#8221;);<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
	using namespace std;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt;    &#8220;Test 1 compiling&#8230;&#8221;      &lt;&lt;endl;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt;    &#8220;Compiling complete, starting Test2&#8243;    &lt;&lt;endl;</p>
<p>	system (&#8220;pause&#8221;);</p>
<p>	Test();</p>
<p>	return 0;<br />
}</p>
<p>________________________________________________</p>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-35428">
		<div id="div-comment-35428" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-35428">
		December 22, 2008 at 11:26 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=35428#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-35428", "35428", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>No.  If a variable is declared in one function, other functions won&#8217;t even know it exists unless you pass it as a parameter.</p>
<p>The reason you are getting an error is because x is declared in main(), so loop() is unaware of it&#8217;s existence.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=38051#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-38051", "38051", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Ravi'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Alex Sir,</p>
<p>I have been observing that whenever you are calling a function,<br />
the function been called has been declared earlier in the program.<br />
Is there any specific reason that a function been called has to be<br />
present before it is been called&#8230;</p>
<p>I mean to say that,</p>
<p>If i call a function named &#8220;doprint2()&#8221; from a function;<br />
&#8220;doprint1()&#8221; and the function &#8220;doprint1()&#8221; has been coded before<br />
the function &#8220;doprint2()&#8221;. And then, i call the function would it affect<br />
it anyway..</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-41968">
		<div id="div-comment-41968" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-41968">
		February 5, 2009 at 10:44 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=41968#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-41968", "41968", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>A function must be declared prior to it&#8217;s use.  However, it does not necessarily need to be <i>defined</i> before use.</p>
<p>In all these examples I declare and define the functions before they are used because it keeps the examples easy.  However, in future lessons, you will learn how to prototype a function so you can both use it and define it anywhere you want.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcf74d619718377-53"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span 		<p>You call DoPrint() twice -- once standalone, and once part of the following cout statement.  Each time DoPrint() is executed, it prints &#8220;In DoPrint()&#8221;, which is why you see it twice.</p>

class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Ending main()"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcf171490711773-19"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fcf171490711773-20"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>

		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251107">
		January 9, 2015 at 4:32 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251107#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251107", "251107", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>If you did that, the using statement would apply to the entire file.  That&#8217;s generally considered bad practice.</p>
<p>By declaring it inside of a function, you limit the effect of the using statement to just the function, which is safer.</p>
		</div>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251112">
		<div id="div-comment-251112" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251112">
		January 9, 2015 at 5:02 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251112#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251112", "251112", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Sometimes.  It&#8217;s a simple question with a complicated answer.</p>
<p>For the programs you are writing now, you can consider main() to be the first function that executes.</p>
<p>There are some cases where other functions can execute before main.  When your program is run, C++ may do some initialization before running main() to get everything set up.  In some cases, this can involve calling other functions before main().</p>
<p>For now, don&#8217;t worry about this.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-95366">
		April 24, 2011 at 4:42 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=95366#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-95366", "95366", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to lynx1241'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>As the text above already stated, <b>some</b> compilers will let you get away with declaring main as void main(). But they will still interpret it as:</p>
<p><code>int main()<br />
{<br />
    // your code here<br />
    return 0;<br />
}</code></p>
<p>Others will just generate an error.</p>

		<p>ok guys quick question<br />
when you run this program why does the words &#8220;Starting DoPrint()&#8221; pop up before &#8220;In DoPrint2()&#8221; even the the DoPrint2()function is listed first?</p>
<p>#include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;<br />
#include </p>
<p>void DoPrint2()<br />
{<br />
    using namespace std;<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In DoPrint2()&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>// Declaration of function DoPrint()<br />
void DoPrint()<br />
{<br />
    using namespace std;<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Starting DoPrint()&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
    DoPrint2(); // This is a function call to DoPrint2()<br />
    DoPrint2(); // This is a function call to DoPrint2()<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Ending DoPrint()&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>// Declaration of main()<br />
int main()<br />
{<br />
    using namespace std;<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Starting main()&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
    DoPrint(); // This is a function call to DoPrint()<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Ending main()&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
    return 0;<br />
}</p>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-95590">
		June 18, 2011 at 10:28 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=95590#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-95590", "95590", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to WordPress'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The becomes virtually unnecessary when it comes to multiple functions being called. The main() function is ALWAYS the first function to start executing even if it may not be the first thing in the source code. Whatever function is called by main() will take action no matter what the order is in the source code. Order only matters inside functions.</p>
		</div>

		<div id="div-comment-251119" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">

		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251119">
		January 9, 2015 at 5:22 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251119#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251119", "251119", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You can only have one return value per function.</p>
<p>However, there are ways to return multiple values.  For example, you can put all your return values in a container and return the container.  Doing this is a little more complicated though, so we don&#8217;t cover that until future lessons.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<p>Why do you use &#8220;using namespace std;&#8221; statement inside each function including main as well? Is there a reason? I think that using the statement as global at once time is more reasonable, isn&#8217;t it? For instance:</p>
<p><code></p>
<p>#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
using namespace std;</p>
<p>void print(){<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;It is going to be written&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>int main(){<br />
  int a = 5;<br />
  cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Value of a: &quot; &lt;&lt; a &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
  return 0;<br />
}</p>
<p><!--formatted--></code></p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251124">
		<div id="div-comment-251124" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251124">
		January 9, 2015 at 5:33 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251124#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251124", "251124", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The operating system needs to know whether your program ran successfully or not.  By convention, main returning a value of zero means success, and a non-zero number means error.</p>
<p>This can be useful when writing a batch file or shell script (outside the scope of these lessons).</p>
		</div>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=207190#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-207190", "207190", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to rameye'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I think it all depends on whether you want to keep your <b>own</b> global namespace for yourself, or give it all up to the <code>std</code> namespace. For these simple examples working solo in the comfort of your local machine it might not be evident, but in the real world you may be competing against the namespaces of many other programmers on a development team, and they can quite possibly be located on remote networks. If code is shared in a common namespace like <code>std</code> then painful name collisions will probably occur.</p>
<p>If you keep your code under your own private namespace, and explicitly qualify names from other namespaces using :: like</p>
<p><code>std::cout</code></p>
<p>all will be well when your code is shared.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		<p>I&#8217;m not sure what you&#8217;re asking.  A few notes:</p>
<p>* std::cout<<&#8221;well done!&#8221;; should be inside main.<br />
* &#8220;x&#8221; shouldn&#8217;t be in quotes since it&#8217;s a variable, not a string.<br />
* You&#8217;re also missing semicolons at the end of most of your lines.<br />
* You can&#8217;t combine a &#8220;using&#8221; statement with a call to std::cout/std::cin.  Do one or the other.</p>

		<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-251534">
		<div id="div-comment-251534" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9eae564a77589e64b80d8a71bbc7db9?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9eae564a77589e64b80d8a71bbc7db9?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Catreece</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251534">
		February 17, 2015 at 9:32 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251534#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251534", "251534", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Catreece'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Ugh, this one gave me a headache when I tried to test it. At first I was setting int = X, then trying to redefine X via a function with X defined within that function. What I&apos;ve discovered is that each function has its own unique value of each variable, so my function can have a completely separate value for X that applies only within that function and is largely irrelevant to the main() function. Yay!</p>
<p>That&apos;s a serious pain in the butt, since it means you have to define each variable within the function you want to actually use it in. It also took me awhile to figure out how to get it to perform the cin within a called function and have the output actually show up where I wanted it in the main() function.</p>
<p>It SORT of made sense, but in a rather twisted way. I&apos;d request an update to this explaining how to use a function to actually return a variable function which is of value, because this wasn&apos;t intuitive in the slightest.</p>
<p>Anyway, here&apos;s what I finally came up with, which fixed the problem.</p>
<p>#include &quot;stdafx.h&quot;<br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;</p>
<p>int SetIntX()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using std::cin;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// set X value to user defined choice<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// testing if x is relevant; believe each variable is unique to their own function<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int n = 0;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; n;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return n; // confirmed; n value meaningless in relation to x<br />
}</p>
<p>int SetIntY()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using std::cin;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// set Y value to user defined choice<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int y = 0;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; y;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return y; // further confirmation; y within function SetIntY() irrelevant to main()<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// set cout to std::cout because I&apos;m lazy :: also test that this statement works properly<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using std::cout;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// test to make sure cin works the way cout does<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using std::cin;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// Also, the above is a test of enclosed comments across multiple lines.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// don&apos;t use the following when calling a function; need to set int X = function<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// int x = 0;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// ditto to int x = 0<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// int y = 0;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// ask user for a number,<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Enter a number: &quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// No initialization takes place; the initial setting is set during the time the function is called<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int x = SetIntX();<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// ask user for a second number<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;You chose &quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; x;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot; as your first number. Enter a second number: &quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// User inputs Y value :: test for second variable and order<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int y = SetIntY();</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// adds totals and displays X+Y :: test for expression<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;You chose &quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; y;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&quot; for your second number, for a combined total of &quot; &lt;&lt; x+y&nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;&lt; std::endl;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return 0;<br />
}</p>
<p>Final output successfully used the functions SetIntX() and SetIntY(), though it required not initializing the values in the first place, which was kind of weird. You&apos;d think it&apos;d just overwrite such, but it won&apos;t let you set the variable X multiple times, or at least not initialize it multiple times. Kind of a nuisance, but it works for now.</p>
<p>Is there an easier way to deal with this? I can see this turning into a horrible mess if there needs to be multiple updates to the value of X.</p>
		</div>

		<p>One challenge with &#8220;working ahead&#8221; is that some of the things you&#8217;re discovering (such as the fact that variables declared in a function only exist within that function) are explictly covered in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/1-4b-a-first-look-at-local-scope/" rel="nofollow">1.4b -- A first look at local scope</a>.</p>
<p>> That&#8217;s a serious pain in the butt, since it means you have to define each variable within the function you want to actually use it in.</p>
<p>Trust me when I say this is a good thing.  If all variables were accessible across multiple functions, you&#8217;d start running into naming conflicts and/or functions could inadvertently change the value of variables they had no business touching!</p>

		<li class="comment even depth-3 clearfix" id="comment-251549">
		<div id="div-comment-251549" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9eae564a77589e64b80d8a71bbc7db9?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9eae564a77589e64b80d8a71bbc7db9?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Catreece</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-251549">
		February 18, 2015 at 7:07 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251549#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251549", "251549", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Catreece'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Yeaaaah&#8230; I discovered that shortly after. =P</p>
<p>I can see the reasoning why you might not want to use variables all over the place to a degree, but honestly, there&apos;s nothing saying you can&apos;t name variables like totalScoreInGameMenu to ensure they&apos;re clearly only used in a single location.</p>
<p>I dunno, just from my time with working with Maya, I really absolutely hate having the same name used in more than one place since sometimes things&apos;ll still break, even if they&apos;re attached to a completely different hierarchy, hence why naming conventions there tend to always have descriptive affixes.</p>
<p>I realize that&apos;s not going to be the same across all programs, nor all languages (though it makes me curious since Maya runs off of Python and MEL, if those languages work the same way as C++ when it comes to naming variables), but it just reaaaaally bothers me to have a variable named X reused in twenty different places, even if none of them know that X exists in any of the other functions. I&apos;d just rather have X consistently and clearly state what X is supposed to represent every time consistently across all functions so I can call on exactly that variable every time I want it.</p>
<p>On the other hand, as you stated, I can see real benefits for keeping variables isolated, especially when it comes to memory management. Not having to store the variable permanently in memory and go looking for it every time you want it is probably rather handy, and utilizing functions to repeat tasks multiple times for different variable outputs means you can use a much smaller program for the same end result.</p>
<p>Well, no point fighting it, and I can see why it&apos;d be rather handy to have, it&apos;ll just take awhile to work through my head that it doesn&apos;t work the same way I&apos;m used to thinking of things. I&apos;ll bet there&apos;s all sorts of handy little tricks that can be done with independent variables like C++ uses, it&apos;ll just take awhile to get used to the idea that X =/= X, except when within the same function.</p>
<p>Also, thanks a ton for the quick replies! The site&apos;s remarkably useful in the first place, and getting quick feedback has been a great help too! ^.^</p>
		</div>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=251677#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251677", "251677", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to AaronHoffman'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>#include &quot;stdafx.h&quot;</p>
<p>int getValueFromUser()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using namespace std;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Enter an integer: &quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int a;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; a;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return a;<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using namespace std;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int x = getValueFromUser(); // first call to getValueFromUser<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int y = getValueFromUser(); // second call to getValueFromUser</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt; &quot; + &quot; &lt;&lt; y &lt;&lt; &quot; = &quot; &lt;&lt; x + y &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return 0;<br />
}<br />
For some reason this wont work, it tells me that cout is not defined :/ even if i try to put it as std::cout it tells me cout / cin / endl isnt usefull for std.<br />
Microsoft visual studio 2013</p>
		</div>

crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd7fe774599441-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">using</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">namespace</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd7fe774599441-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Enter an integer: "</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd7fe774599441-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">a</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd7fe774599441-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">cin</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">a</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd7fe774599441-8"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">a</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd7fe774599441-9"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0012 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this function, on line 6, we define an integer variable named &#8216;a&#8217;.  On line 7, we read input from the user and place it in variable &#8216;a&#8217;.  And on line 8, we return the value that was placed in variable &#8216;a&#8217; to the caller of the function (who can do whatever they want with it).</p>
<p>Return 0 would always return the value 0 to the caller, but that&#8217;s not what we want in this case.  Instead, we want the function to return the user&#8217;s inputted value to the caller, so we return the value of variable a.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fcd11a797355628-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd11a797355628-1">&nbsp;</div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>#include &lt;iostream&gt;</p>
<p>// void means the function does not return a value to the caller<br />
void returnNothing()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// This function does not return a value so no return statement is needed<br />
}</p>
<p>// int means the function returns an integer value to the caller<br />
int return5()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return 5; // this function returns an integer, so a return statement is needed<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using namespace std;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; return5(); // prints 5<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; return5() + 2; // prints 7<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;//cout &lt;&lt; returnNothing(); // This line will not compile.&nbsp;&nbsp;You&#8217;ll need to comment it out to continue.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;returnNothing(); // okay: function returnNothing() is called, no value is returned<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return5(); // okay: function return5() is called, return value is discarded<br />
}</p>
<p>//why does it tell me 57? lol anyone?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252472">
		<div id="div-comment-252472" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/#comment-252472">
		May 15, 2015 at 11:18 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/?replytocom=252472#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252472", "252472", "respond", "23" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The key are these two lines:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d746fcd055408768992" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fcd055408768992-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d746fcd055408768992-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd055408768992-1"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">return5</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// prints 5</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d746fcd055408768992-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">return5</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">2</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// prints 7</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>We&#8217;ve defined return5() to return the value 5.<br />
On the first line, return5() returns 5.  We then send this value to cout to be printed.  So what appears on your screen is &#8220;5&#8221;.<br />
On the second line, return5() returns 5, and then we add 2 to get 7.  We then send this value to cout to be printed.  So what appears on your screen is &#8220;7&#8221;.</p>
<p>Because we didn&#8217;t print any spaces between them, the &#8220;5&#8221; and the &#8220;7&#8221; get run together, so it looks like &#8220;57&#8221;.</p>
<p>It sounds like you&#8217;re treating &#8220;57&#8221; as a single number.  But what&#8217;s happening is we&#8217;re printing the digit 5, and then printing the digit 7, with no space between them.  Hence, what gets printed is &#8220;57&#8221;.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
